919. What does mean hyperkeratosis?

excessive thickening of the stratum corneum of the epithelium; *
disturbances of cornification of individual epithelium cells;
accumulation of fluid within cells of basal and spiny layers;
intercellular edema between the keratinocytes in the epidermis.


920. What is typical for dyskeratosis?
excessive formation of keratin when the granular and spiny layers get thicker;
granular layer is absent, the stratum corneum gets thicker and its cells contain bacilliform nucleus. Clinically it is manifested turbidity mucosal epithelium;
individual epithelial cells are enlarged, rounded: nucleus intensely colored, cytoplasm is eosinophilic, slightly granular. These cells lose intercellular contacts and randomly arranged in most layers of the epithelium; *
as a result of fluid accumulation in spiny layer, the size of cells increases, the nucleus changes the shape and size and then splits to form single-cell cavity;
the cavities filled with fluid are formed as a result of certain areas of colliquative necrosis of the epithelium in the mouth and have cells that resemble balloons.

1482. What is the procedure of balanced force technique in RCT?
The file is placed to working length and rotated clockwise 900 with light pressure to engage dentin; then file is rotated counterclockwise 1200 while apical pressure is maintained to cut and enlarge the canal. *
After determining the WL, the first active instrument to be inserted should be fine small sized, 0,02 tapered, stainless steel file; once the apical preparation is complete, Gates Glidden are used to further funnel the preparation coronally.
At first H-file № 15, 20 is penetrated root canal; then Gates Glidden drills flaring the coronal segment of root canal is used; then shaping the remaining canal in crown-down approach, using decreasing size of instruments in sequence.
After pulp removal with barbed broaches, root canal instrumentation is carried out only with small sized reamers and K-type files.
We should use only one instrument for maximal saving of hard tissues.


1483. What is the procedure of step-back technique in RCT?
After determining the WL, the first active instrument to be inserted should be fine small sized, 0,02 tapered, stainless steel file; once the apical preparation is complete, Gates Glidden are used to further funnel the preparation coronally. *
The file is placed to working length and rotated clockwise 900 with light pressure to engage dentin; then file is rotated counterclockwise 1200 while apical pressure is maintained to cut and enlarge the canal.
At first H-file № 15, 20 is penetrated root canal; then Gates Glidden drills flaring the coronal segment of root canal is used; then shaping the remaining canal in crown-down approach, using decreasing size of instruments in sequence.
After pulp removal with barbed broaches, root canal instrumentation is carried out only with small sized reamers and K-type files.
The first file should be rotary.


1484. What is the procedure of crown-down technique in RCT?
At first H-file № 15, 20 is penetrated root canal; then Gates Glidden drills flaring the coronal segment of root canal is used; then shaping the remaining canal in crown-down approach, using decreasing size of instruments in sequence. *
The file is placed to working length and rotated clockwise 900 with light pressure to engage dentin; then file is rotated counterclockwise 1200 while apical pressure is maintained to cut and enlarge the canal.
After determining the WL, the first active instrument to be inserted should be fine small sized, 0,02 tapered, stainless steel file; once the apical preparation is complete, Gates Glidden are used to further funnel the preparation coronally.
After pulp removal with barbed broaches, root canal instrumentation is carried out only with small sized reamers and K-type files.
The first file should be rotary.
